Jamison Brereton

51
Indra
Savya ─Ас╣Еgirasa
15 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 14тАУ15
This hymn consists primarily of an elaborated list of IndraтАЩs great deeds, some well known (like the Vala myth in 3a, the Vr╠еtra myth in 4, IndraтАЩs involvement164 I.51
with U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya and Kutsa in the slaying of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa in verses 6a, 10тАУ11) and others quite obscure. For example, Vimada, mentioned in 3ab, is usually a client of the A┼Ыvins, who supply him with a wife (often using the same verb [тИЪvah тАЬcon veyтАЭ] as here: I.112.9, 116.1, 117.20; X.39.7, 65.12). Is the same deed attributed to Indra here and is the тАЬgood thingтАЭ that Indra brings him a reference to the wife? Similarly puzzling are the enemies who make oblation тАЬon the shoulderтАЭ in verse 5 (perhaps indicating people following different ritual practices and not part of the ─Аrya community; see vss. 8тАУ9), IndraтАЩs role as an ant destroying walls in verse 9, and his transformation into the female consort of an otherwise unknown figure in verse 13c.
The catalogue of deeds is interrupted by demands that Indra use his same mar tial powers for our benefit (vss. 7тАУ9ab), and it is framed by an exhortation to the poets to give praise to the god (vs. 1) and the announcement of the end of the praise hymn and the boons we seek from it (vss. 14тАУ15).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAnime with praises that ram, (Indra), who is adored by many, who is gratified by hymns, and is an ocean of wealth; whose good deeds spread abroad for the benefit of mankind, like the rays of light; worship the powerful and wise Indra, for the enjoyment of prosperity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tyam. meс╣гam: Indra assumed the form of a ram and came to a sacrifice performed by Medh─Бtithi and drank Soma, so a legend;

Meс╣гa = victor over foes. Another legend is that Aс╣Еgiras worshipped to get a son who would resemble Indra; Indra himself became his son whose name was Savya

Jamison Brereton

With your hymns exhilarate this ram, much-summoned Indra worthy of verses, the flood of good,
for whom the human (generations) pass by like the days. Chant to the most liberal inspired one for our benefit.

Griffith

MAKE glad with songs that Ram whom many men invoke, worthy of songs of praise, Indra, the sea of wealth;
Whose gracious deeds for men spread like the heavens abroad: sing praise to him the Sage, most liberal for our good.

Geldner

Den bekannten Widder, den vielgerufenen, preisw├╝rdigen Indra erg├╢tzet mit Lobreden, der ein Sturm des Guten ist; f├╝r den die menschlichen Geschlechter wie die Tage vergehen. Den freigebigsten Redekundigen besinget euch zu Nutz!

Grassmann

Erfreut mit Lied den vielgerufnen Widder, ihn, den preisenswerthen Indra, der ein Meer des Guts; Ihn, dessen Tage nicht vergehn wie menschliche, der zum Genuss am meisten schenkt, den weisen preist.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe protecting and fostering с╣Ъbhus hastened to the presence of Indra, of graceful motion, and irradiating the firmament, imbued with vigour, the humiliator of his enemies, the performer of a hundred pious acts; and by them, encouraging words were uttered.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъbhus = Maruts who encouraged Indra; ‘all gods who were your friends have fled; may there be friendship between the Maruts and you’. Indra is one of 12 ─Аdityas, as ┼Ъakra, hence ‘irradiating the firmament’; words were uttered: prahara bhagava v─лryasva, strike; bhagavan, be valiant

Jamison Brereton

His forms of help [=helpers] attained to the very superior one, who fills the midspace but is enclosed by his powersтАФ
the skillful R╠еbhus (attained to) Indra, who was aroused to
exhilaration. Liberality, impelling (him), mounted to him of a
hundred resolves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse displays a type of тАЬpoetic repairтАЭ: the first hemistich has a grammatical subject that is ordinarily inanimate (┼лt├бyaс╕е тАШ[forms of] helpтАЩ) with a verb that ought to have a personal subject (abh├н .. avanvan тАШthey attained to / gainedтАЩ), with an object possessing a number of qualities, but unnamed; the third p─Бda solves this slight puzzle by giving names to both: the subject is the с╣Ъbhus, the object Indra.

The spatial contrast in b between filling the midpace, but being himself enclosed by his own powers (muscle-bound?) is nice.

j├бvana- occurs only here in the RV, but the -ana-suffix ordinarily makes transitive nominals (pace GeldnerтАЩs тАЬraschhandeln,тАЭ RenouтАЩs тАЬv├йloceтАЭ).

Griffith

As aids the skilful Rbhus yearned to Indra strong to save, who fills mid-air, encompassed round with might,
Rushing in rapture; and o’er Satakratu came the gladdening shout that urged him on to victory.

Ihn, den ├Ьberlegenen, bevorzugten die Hilfen, der den Luftraum ausf├╝llt, der von den St├дrken umgeben ist, den rauscherregten Indra, die geschickten Ribhu┬┤s. Zu dem Ratreichen ist die raschhandelnde Gro├Яmut aufgestiegen.

Grassmann

Der gerne beisteht, kraftbegabt die Luft erf├╝llt, den Indra haben die Gen├╝sse recht erfreut, Den Rauscherregten kunstge├╝bt die S├дngerschar, zum hundertkr├дft’gen steigt ermunternd der Gesang.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have opened the cloud for the Aс╣Еgirasas you have shown the way to Atri, who vexes his adversaries by a hundred doors (by a number of yantras, means or contrivances); you have granted wealth, with food, to Vimada; you are wielding your thunderbolt in defence of a worshipper engaged in battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Gotra = herd of cattle or a cloud;

Gotrabhid = mountain-breaker with his thunderbolt (Indra) or may allude to the recovery of cows stolen by Paс╣Зi;;

Vimada = a maharс╣гi

Jamison Brereton

You opened up the cowpen for the Aс╣Еgirases, and you were the
way-finder for Atri in the (house) of a hundred doors.
You also conveyed the good thing [=wife?] to Vimada along with grain (for the oblation?), when in the contest you set to dancing the stone of the one clad in it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though the verse starts promisingly, with two identifiable myths (Vala, p─Бda a; Atri, p─Бda b – though the 100-doored [house] is not otherwise known), the second hemistich brings obscurity. As noted in the introduction, the standard myth about Vimada involves the A┼Ыvins bringing him a wife, usually with the verb (n├н) тИЪvah. Is this the same story, with v├бsu тАШgood thingтАЩ a generic substitution for тАШwifeтАЩ, or is IndraтАЩs relationship with Vimada of a different sort from the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ? As for p─Бda d, the action here is completely obscure (see GeldnerтАЩs somewhat desperate note attempting to make this about a rocky nest [Felsennest] of robbers), and what it has to do with the Vimada story is equally obscure. Since nart├бyan in d is only a participle, it should be attached to the main clause in c rather than relating a separate myth. A final bit of obscurity is sas├йna тАШwith grainтАЩ, which opens c. The stem sas├б- generally shows up in enigmatic phrases referring, probably, to the ritual grass and/or the cereal ritual oblations.

Griffith

Thou hast disclosed the kine’s stall for the Angirases, and made a way for Atri by a hundred doors.
On Vimada thou hast bestowed both food and wealth, making thy bolt dance in the sacrificer’s fight.

Geldner

Du hast f├╝r die Angira┬┤s die Kuhherde aufgedeckt und dem Atri warst du Pfadfinder in dem hunderttorigen Hause. Dem Vimada brachtest du Gutes sogar auf Vorrat, indem du im Kampfe den Fels des, der sich darin einh├╝llte verbarg, im Kreise drehtest.

Grassmann

Den Angiras hast du den Kuhstall aufgethan dem Atri auch, durch hundert Th├╝ren schaffend Bahn; Hast selbst im Schlafe Gut dem Vimada gebracht, als du im Kampf den Stein des Sch├╝tzen schleudertest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have opened the receptacle of the waters; you have detained in the mountain the treasure of the malignant; when you had slain Vс╣Ыtra, the destryer, you made the sun visible in the sky.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Parvate danumad vasu = in the mountain, a dwelling of Indra;

Danumad = descended from Danu, a D─Бnava, an asura or an epithet of vasu, wealth, fit for liberality (from danu, giving) or one doing injury, an enemy; Vс╣Ыtra (Ahi) is hantri, the slayer; so yat sarv─Бn etat samabhavat tasm─Бd ahiriti, inasmuch as he was the same as all that (benefits of sacrifice, fame, knowledge, prosperity), he wa called Ahi

Jamison Brereton

You opened up the covers of the waters; you held fast to the drop-laden goods in the mountain.
When, o Indra, with your vast power you smashed the serpent Vr╠еtra, just after that you made the sun rise in heaven to be seen.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse, by contrast, clearly concerns the Vс╣Ыtra myth and is for the most part unchallenging. It is worth noting that its first p─Бda is structured almost exactly like 3a and begins and ends identically: tv├бm тАж (a)vс╣Ыс╣Зor ├бpa. The verse also contains an occurrence of v├бsu (in b), which unfortunately doesnтАЩt shed any light on the mysterious v├бsu in 3c. In fact 4b is the only part of this verse that is somewhat unclear: the d─Б╠Бnumad v├бsu (тАШdrop-laden goodsтАЩ, taking d─Б╠Бnu to тАШdropтАЩ with Grassmann and Renou, rather than тАШgiftтАЩ with Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н]) is of course the water confined in the mountain by Vс╣Ыtra, which Indra releases. But why does Indra hold it fast (├бdh─Бrayaс╕е) in the mountain rather than releasing it as usual? The passage is similar to the Indra ─Бtmastuti X.49.9 ah├бс╣Г sapt├б srav├бto dh─Бrayaс╣Г vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б. Perhaps he gave the waters, as it were, emotional support - but this doesn’t sound like either the Rigveda or Indra.

At best weтАЩre left with an attenuated meaning like тАЬhelp out.тАЭ Or тАФ a long shot тАФ this is an expression like I.103.7 sas├бntaс╣Г тАж abodhay├│ тАШhim тАЬyou тАШawakenedтАЩ the sleeping serpent,тАЭ where abodhayaс╕е is meant to evoke its opposite, тАШput to sleepтАЩ.

See introduction. to that hymn and Jamison 1982/83. In that case тАШhold fastтАЩ would evoke тАШlet goтАЩ. For a possibly similar passage with Indra тАЬbringing to restтАЭ the waters rather than releasing them, see V.32.1 and comm. thereto. However, the formulaic nexus between тИЪbudh тАШawakeтАЩ and тИЪsas / svap тАШsleepтАЩ is very strong, whereas тИЪdhс╣Ы is not regularly paired with, say, forms of тИЪsс╣Ыj тАШreleaseтАЩ, and so I advance this possibility only very tentatively. Elizabeth Tucker offers another intriguing suggestion. She cites the wellknown Oldenberg Persian PN D─Бraya-vahu (corresponding phonologically to Skt.

*dh─Бr├бya- + v├бsu, and wonders тАЬCould the poet be deliberately using, perhaps even punning on, an inherited Indo-Iranian collocation of the verb *dhс╣Ы with object *v├бsu?тАЭ

Griffith

Thou hast unclosed the prisons of the waters; thou hast in the mountain seized the treasure rich in gifts.
When thou hadst slain with might the dragon Vrtra, thou, Indra, didst raise the Sun in heaven for all to see.

Geldner

Du hast die Verschl├╝sse der Gew├дsser ge├╢ffnet; du hieltest fest den Schatz der Himmelsgabe in dem Berge. Als du, Indra, den Drachen mit aller Kraft erschlagen hattest, da lie├Яest du am Himmel die Sonne zum Schauen aufsteigen.

Grassmann

Der Wasserflut Verschl├╝sse hast du aufgethan, und hast im Berg das tropfenreiche Gut bewahrt; Als Indra du den Vritra-drachen schlugst mit Macht, da liessest hoch am Himmel du die Sonne schaun.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Indra, by the devices, have humbled the deceivers who presented oblations to their own mouths; propitious to men, you have destroyed the cities of Pipru, and have well defended с╣Ъji┼Ыvan in robber-destroying (contest).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Pipru is an asura; с╣Ъji┼Ыvan is a worshipper whom they oppressed; dasyu-hatye┼Ыu, in battles killing the dasyus

Jamison Brereton

With your wiles you blew away the wily ones, who, according to their own customs, poured (their offering) тАЬon the shoulder.тАЭ
You broke through the strongholds of Pipru, o you of manly mind; you helped R╠еji┼Ыvan through in the smashing of Dasyus.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note alliteration: тАж pipror тАж pr─Б╠Бrujaс╕е p├║raс╕е, pr├б тАж

Griffith

With wondrous might thou blewest enchanter fiends away, with powers celestial those who called on thee in jest.
Thou, hero-hearted, hast broken down Pipru’s forts, and helped Rjisvan when the Dasyus were struck dead.

Geldner

Du bliesest mit Zauberk├╝nsten die Zauberkundigen hinweg, die nach eigenem Ermessen ├╝ber die Schulter opferten. Du brachst des Pipru Burgen, du Mannherziger; du halfst dem Rijisvan in den Dasyuschlachten weiter.

Grassmann

Du bliesest weg die Zauberer mit Zaubermacht, die eignen Brauches auf der Schulter opferten; Des Pipru Burgen brachest heldenm├╝th’ger du, und halfest dem Ridschi├зvan im D├дmonenkampf.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have defended Kutsa in fatal fights with ┼Ъu┼Ыna; you have destroyed ┼Ъambara in defence of Atithigva; you have trodden with your foot upon the great Arbuda; frm remote times were you born for the destruction of oppressors.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъu┼Ыna, ┼Ъambara and Arbuda are asuras. Kutsa is a с╣Ыс╣гi;

Atithigva = hospitable, Divod─Бsa

Jamison Brereton

You helped Kutsa in the smashing of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa, and you made ┼Ъambara subject to Atithigva.
With your foot you trampled down Arbuda, though he was great.
Indeed, from long ago you were born to smash Dasyus.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Jesse Lundquist cleverly suggests that the verse contains a word play on the PN of IndraтАЩs defeated opponent Arbuda: by characterizing him as тАШgreatтАЩ (mah─Б╠Бnt-), the poet implicitly evokes the semantic opposite ├бrbha-, arbhak├б-, which resembles the PN phonologically and would help regularize the non-IndoAryan -b- in arbud├б. So, тАЬyou trampled down Arbuda (the little one), though he was great.тАЭ As Jesse Lundquist points out, support for this interpretation comes from 13a ├бdad─Б ├бrbh─Бm mahat├й тАж, kakс╣г─л╠Бvate vс╣Ыcay─Б╠Бm тАж тАЬYou gave little Vс╣Ыcay─Б to great Kakс╣г─лvant.

Griffith

Thou savedst Kutsa when Susna was smitten down; to Atithigva gavest Sambara for a prey.
E’en mighty Arbuda thou troddest under foot: thou from of old wast born to strike the Dasyus dead.

Geldner

Du standest dem Kutsa in den Susnak├дmpfen bei, du liefertest dem Atithigva den Sambara aus. Den Arbuda tratest du trotz seiner Gr├╢├Яe mit dem Fu├Яe nieder. Vor alters schon bist du f├╝r die Dasyuerschlagung geboren.

Grassmann

Du halfst dem Kutsa, als er mit D├дmonen focht, und gabst in Atithigva’s Hand den ├Зambara, Mit F├╝ssen tratest du den grossen Arbuda, Und Unholdt├╢dtung bist von Anfang du bestimmt.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН рд╡реАрд░ ! рдпрддрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдкрджрд╛ рдкрджрд╛рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕рдореВрд╣рдВ рдЪрд┐рджрд┐рд╡ рд╢реБрд╖реНрдгрд╣рддреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рдпреБрджреНрдзреЗрд╖реБ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдХреБрддреНрд╕рдВ рдзреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдЖрд╡рд┐рде рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдирд░рдиреНрдзрдпреЛрд╜рддрд┐рдерд┐рдЧреНрд╡рд╛рдп рд╢реБрджреНрдзрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдпрд╛рд░реНрдмреБрджрдВ рд╢рдореНрдмрд░рдВ рдмрд▓рдВ рдирд┐рдХреНрд░рдореАрдГ рд╕рдирд╛рддреНрдкрджрд╛ рджрд╕реНрдпреБрд╣рддреНрдпрд╛рдпреИрд╡ рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рд╖реЗ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпреЛрд╜рд╕рд┐ рее рем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░рдкрд┐ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдЧреБрдгрд╛ рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn you, Indra, is all vigour fully concentrated; you will delight to drink the Soma; it is known by us that the thunderbolt is deposited in your hands; cut off all prowess from the foe.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In you every power has been placed toward the same end. Your
generosity excites itself to drink the soma. Your mace has become visible, placed in your arms: hew down the
bullish strengths of your rival.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrasing of p─Бda b is conceptually backwards, strikingly so. Ordinarily Indra drinks the soma and is moved to be generous, whereas here his (latent) generosity rouses itself in anticipation of the soma.

v├н┼Ыv─Бni carelessly omitted in published translation: тАЬall the bullish strengths.тАЭ More alliteration: vс╣Ы┼Ыc─Б╠Б┼Ы├бtror ├бva v├н┼Ыv─Бni vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гny─Б, with sequences of v with either i or с╣Ы, followed by ┼Ы or с╣г (with a few more vтАЩs and a ┼Ы thrown in).

Griffith

All power and might is closely gathered up in thee; thy bounteous spirit joys in drinking Soma juice.
Known is the thunderbolt that lies within thine arms: rend off therewith all manly prowess of our foe.

Geldner

In dich ist alle St├дrke insgesamt gelegt; deine Freigebigkeit freut sich auf den Somatrunk. Deine Keule tut sich hervor, wenn sie dir in die Arme gelegt wird. Beschneide alle Kr├дfte des Feindes!

Grassmann

In dich sind alle Kr├дfte insgesammt gelegt; dein holder Sinn erfreut sich an dem Somatrunk, Es zeigt der Blitz sich, der in deinen Armen ruht, des Feindes Kr├дfte haue alle du herab.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬDiscriminate between the ─Аryas and they who are Dasyus; restraining those who perform no religious rites, compel them to submit to the performer of sacrifices; be you, who are powerful, the encourager of the sacrificer; I am desirous of celebrating all your deeds in ceremonies that give you satisfaction.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

─Аryas are those who practise religious rites; Dasyus do not observe religious ceremonies and inimical to those who do

Jamison Brereton

Distinguish between the ─Аryas and those who are Dasyus. Chastising those who follow no commandment, make them subject to the man who provides ritual grass.
Become the potent inciter of the sacrificer. I take pleasure in all these (deeds) of yours at our joint revelries.

Griffith

Discern thou well Aryas and Dasyus; punishing the lawless give them up to him whose grass is strewn.
Be thou the sacrificer’s strong encourager all these thy deeds are my delight at festivals.

Geldner

Unterscheide zwischen den Ariern und den Dasyu┬┤s; die Unbotm├д├Яigen z├╝chtigend mache sie dem Opferer untertan! Mach dich stark, sei Ermutiger des Opfernden! An all diesem Tun von dir habe ich bei den Somagelagen meine Freude.

Grassmann

Barbaren unterscheide wohl und Arier, dem Frommen liefre strafend aus, die gottlos sind, Als starker F├╢rdrer zeige dich des opfernden; dies alles m├╢cht’ bei deinen Mahlen ich empfahn.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп ! рддреВ (рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖реНрдорддреЗ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рджрд┐ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдХреА рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЖрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдиреН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░рдХ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрд╣рд┐) рдЬрд╛рди рдФрд░ (рдпреЗ) рдЬреЛ (рджрд╕реНрдпрд╡рдГ) рдкрд░рдкреАреЬрд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЕрдзрд░реНрдореА рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрдирдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рди рдХрд░ (рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖реНрдорддреЗ) рдзрд░реНрдо рдХреА рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд░рдиреНрдзрдп) рдорд╛рд░ рдФрд░ рдЙрди (рдЕрд╡реНрд░рддрд╛рдиреН) рд╕рддреНрдпрднрд╛рд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐ рдзрд░реНрдорд░рд╣рд┐рдд рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╢рд╛рд╕рддреН) рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХреЗ рдХрд░реНрддрд╛ рдХрд╛ (рдЪреЛрджрд┐рддрд╛) рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдгрд╛рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛ рдФрд░ (рд╢рд╛рдХреА) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдп рдХреЛ (рднрд╡) рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд░, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░реЗ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧ рд╕реЗ (рд╕рдзрдорд╛рджреЗрд╖реБ) рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рддрд╛) рдЙрди (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛) рд╕рдм рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреА (рдЗрддреН) рд╣реА рдореИрдВ (рдЪрд╛рдХрди) рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реВрдБ рее рео рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рджрд╕реНрдпреБ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рдХреЛ рдЫреЛреЬ рдХрд░ рдЖрд░реНрдпреНрдп рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдп рд╕реЗ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗред рд╡реЗ рд╣реА рдЖрд░реНрдп рд╣реИрдВ рдХрд┐ рдЬреЛ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ рд╕рдмрдХреЗ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рднреЛрдЧ рдХреА рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ рдФрд░ рдЕрдзрд░реНрдореА рджреБрд╖реНрдЯреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдг рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдпрддреНрди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдХреЛрдИ рднреА рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЖрд░реНрдпреНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдВрдЧ, рдЙрдирд╕реЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрдпрди рд╡рд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рдпрдерд╛рд╡рддреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН, рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛, рдЖрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдХреЛ рд╕рдорд░реНрде рдирд╣реАрдВ рд╣реЛ рд╕рдХрддрд╛ред рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдЖрд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рдФрд░ рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕реЗрд╡рди рдХрд░ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рд╕реБрдЦреА рд░рд╣рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рео рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп ! рддреНрд╡рдВ рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖реНрдордд рдЖрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрд╣рд┐ рдпреЗ рджрд╕реНрдпрд╡рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдБрд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд┐рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд░рдиреНрдзрдпрд╛рд╜рд╡реНрд░рддрд╛рдиреН рд╢рд╛рд╕рддреН рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдЪреЛрджрд┐рддрд╛ рд╕рдиреН рд╢рд╛рдХреА рднрд╡ рдпрддрд╕реНрддреЗ рддрд╡реЛрдкрджреЗрд╢реЗрди рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреЗрди рд╡рд╛ рд╕рдзрдорд╛рджреЗрд╖реБ рддрд╛ рддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдпреЗрддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреАрджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╣рдВ рдЪрд╛рдХрди рее рео рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд┐) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереЗ (рдЬрд╛рдиреАрд╣рд┐) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ (рдЖрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдиреН) рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХрд╛рдирд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░рдХрд╛рдиреН рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреН (рдпреЗ) рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛рдГ (рдЪ) рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗ (рджрд╕реНрдпрд╡рдГ) рдкрд░рдкреАрдбрдХрд╛ рдореВрд░реНрдЦрд╛ рдзрд░реНрдорд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖реНрдорддреЗ) рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд╛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рджрдпреЛ рдЧреБрдгрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗ рддрдиреНрдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрддреНрддрдпреЗ (рд░рдиреНрдзрдп) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдп (рд╢рд╛рд╕рддреН) рд╢рд╛рд╕рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНред (рдЕрд╡реНрд░рддрд╛рдиреН) рд╕рддреНрдпрднрд╛рд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдиреН (рд╢рд╛рдХреА) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдГ рд╢рд╛рдХрдГ рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдГ (рднрд╡) рдирд┐рд░реНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд╕реНрд╡ (рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп) рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдХрд╕реНрдп (рдЪреЛрджрд┐рддрд╛) рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдХрдГ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рддрд╛) рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╕рдзрдорд╛рджреЗрд╖реБ) рд╕реБрдЦреЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗрд╖реБ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╖реБ (рдЪрд╛рдХрди) рдХрд╛рдордпреЗред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдХрдирдзрд╛рддреЛрд░реНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд▓рд┐рдЯреН рддреБрдЬрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рджреАрд░реНрдШреЛрд╜рднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╕реНрдп (рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрд╛режрем.рез.рен) рдЗрддреНрдпрднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рджреАрд░реНрдШрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЪ рее рео рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra abides, humbling the neglecters of holy acts in favour of those who observe them; and punishing those who turn away from his worship in favour of those who are present (with their praise); Vamra, while praising him, whether old or adolescent, and spreading through heaven, carried off the accusative ulated (materials of the sacrifice).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vamro vijagh─Бna samdihaс╕е = vamra destryed the collections. Vamra, a с╣Ыс╣гi, when Indra was absent, carried away the accusative ulated heap of offerings, the marrow or essence of the earth, yad valmika-vap_sambh─Бro bhavati ┼лrjjam eva pс╣Ыthivy─Бс╕е

Jamison Brereton

IndraтАФmaking those who reject his commandments subject to those who follow his commandments, piercing those who donтАЩt stand by
him with (the aid of) those who doтАФ
being praised, as an ant he smashed apart the mud walls of the one trying to reach heaven, who, though already full grown, kept
growing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The avrat├б- тАШhaving no commandmentтАЩ of 8b is transformed into the even less savory ├бpavrata- тАШagainst/rejecting commandmentsтАЩ and contrasted with their opposite number, the ├бnuvrata- тАШfollowing commandmentsтАЩ.

The image of IndraтАЩs transformation into an ant (vamr├б-) presumably concerns his ability to pass unnoticed in the enemy camp and then bring the fortifications down from within. However, тАЬsmashing apartтАЭ (v├н тИЪhan) doesn’t seem a likely action for an ant, or even a huge nest of ants, so the combined image is somewhat unsettled.

The identity of the enemy in this hemistich is not clear. The other occurrence of the phrase dy─Б╠Бm ├нnakс╣гant- (X.45.7) refers to Agni, but that identification seems unlikely here. It should also be noted that the other genitive phrase referring to this enemy, vс╣Ыddh├бsya cid v├бrdhataс╕е тАЬthe one who, though already full grown, kept growing,тАЭ is grammatically problematic because the active present participle v├бrdhant- should be transitive, as the rest of this extremely well-attested active inflection is. Got┼Н (1987: 291) notes the problem but has no explanation either.

Expected middle *v├бrdham─Бnasya would of course not fit this metrical position, but that is not enough for a Rigvedic poet to contravene grammar. However, the active part. more nearly matches the paired ppl. phonologically: vс╣ЫddhaтАж vardhaтАж, and this may have influenced the poet to use the active form.

Griffith

Indra gives up the lawless to the pious man, destroying by the Strong Ones those who have no strength.
Vamra when glorified destroyed the gathered piles of the still waxing great one who would reach the heaven.

Geldner

Indra ist der, welcher die Unbotm├д├Яigen untertan macht, der mit seinen Anh├дngern die Gegner niederst├╢├Яt. Als Ameise zerschmi├Я der Gepriesene die Mauern des den Himmel Erstrebenden, der schon ausgewachsen noch weiter wuchs.

Grassmann

Die Ungerechten gibt er dem Gerechten preis, durch Treue tilget Indra die, die untreu sind; Dem grossen, der noch w├дchst, zum Himmel reicht, hat Vamra r├╝hmlich seine W├дlle umgest├╝rzt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIf Uс╣гan─Бs should sharpen your vigour by his own, then would your might terrify by its intensity both heaven and earth. Friend of man, let the will harnessed steeds, with the velocity of the wind, convey you, replete (with vigour), to (partake of the sacrificial) food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When U┼Ыan─Б fashions might with might for you, then your vast power thrusts apart the two worlds with its greatness.
The mind-yoked (horses) of the Wind conveyed you, being filled (with soma?), here to fame, o manly minded one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A nice adjacency figure, nс╣Ыmaс╣Зo manoyujaс╕е.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) supplies тАЬwith strengthтАЭ with p┼л╠Бryam─Бnam тАШbeing filledтАЩ, but RenouтАЩs тАЬwith somaтАЭ (an alternative allowed by Geldner in his n.) seems more likely on the basis of other тАЬfillтАЭ phrases involving Indra. Esp. apposite is V.34.2, adduced by Geldner, where Indra fills his belly with soma while U┼Ыan─Б offers him a weapon, much as here.

IndraтАЩs exhilaration in the immediately following verse here (11a) also supports the soma interpretation.

Griffith

The might which Usana hath formed for thee with might rends in its greatness and with strength both worlds apart.
O Hero-souled, the steeds of Vata, yoked by thought, have carried thee to fame while thou art filled with power.

Geldner

Als Usanas dir mit Kraft die Kraft zimmerte, da sprengte deine Gewalt durch ihre Gr├╢├Яe die beiden Welth├дlften auseinander. Dich fuhren, du Mannherziger, des Vata Rosse, die durch blo├Яen Gedanken umherschwirrten, zur Ruhmestat, als du mit Kraft angef├╝llt warst.

Grassmann

Wenn U├зana aus Kraft dir neue Kraft erzeugt dr├дngt Erd’ und Himmel weithin kr├дftig deine Macht, Dich fuhren her des Windes Rosse, geistgeschirrt, o heldenm├╝th’ger Somatrinker, dich zum Ruhm.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen Indra is delighted with acceptable hymns, he ascends (his car), drawn by more and more obliquely-curving coursers; fierce, he extracts the waters from the passing (cloud) in a torrent, and has overwhelmed the extensive cities of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When he has found exhilaration together with U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya, Indra mounts the two (horses) that are surging and surging further.
The strong one let loose the waters in a stream for coursing and
propelled apart the fortified strongholds of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa.

Jamison Brereton Notes

vaс╣Еk┼л╠Бvaс╣Еkut├бr─Б is generally taken as characterizing the speed of the two horses, and I agree that that is the general idea – but think this meaning arises indirectly. Geldner takes it as тАШflyingтАЩ, Renou as тАШrapidтАЩ, Hoffmann (Inj. 221) тАШever faster movingтАЩ, Witzel Got┼Н тАШever faster gallopingтАЩ, but this basic meaning does not fit the root to which it most likely belongs, тИЪva├▒c тАШmove crookedlyтАЩ, or the other occurrences of vaс╣Еk├║-, esp. I.114.4. I think the nuance here is the same one found in the deriv. adj.

v├бkva(n)- тАШbillowingтАЩ ├а тАШsurgingтАЩ. The non-linear movement of the root is here concretized as a wave motion, with the attendant speed and power associated with waves.

The c p─Бda presents some difficulties of construction, particularly the two accusatives yay├нm and ap├бс╕е, which do not match in number. Geldner and Renou supply тАШmountsтАЩ (├бdhi tiс╣гс╣нhati) from the end of p─Бda b (or perhaps ─Б╠БтАж tiс╣гс╣нhasi from 12a) and тАШchariotтАЩ with yay├нm and begin a new clause with n├нr. So, тАЬthe powerful one (mounted) the speeding (chariot); he released the water in a stream.тАЭ Alternatively Geldner suggests that c is a single clause, but that ap├бс╕е is not an acc. pl., as is usual, but the rare gen. sg. construed with sr├│tas─Б, so тАЬthe powerful one released the speeding (chariot) with the waterтАЩs stream(speed) [mit des Wassers Strom(schnelle)].тАЭ Neither of these fussy solutions is appealing. With regard to the latter, nir ap├бс╕е [acc.pl.] тИЪsс╣Ыj appears to be formulaic (cf. I.103.2, X.124.7, the only other examples of n├нс╕е тИЪsс╣Ыj that I know of), and so a gen. sg. is unlikely; with regard to the former, it seems overly elaborate to supply so much material in a p─Бda that can be read as a unity. I follow Oldenberg in taking yay├нm as an epithet of (so Oldenberg) or, better, an appositive or qualifier to the waters. Since ├бp- тАШwater(s)тАЩ is in essence a plurale tantum, a parallel singular would not be surprising. For yay├н/─л╠Б- qualifying waters, cf. X.78.7 s├нndhavo n├б yay├нyaс╕е тАЬcoursing like rivers,тАЭ adduced by Oldenberg (also X.92.5). My tr. тАЬfor coursingтАЭ rather than тАЬas coursingтАЭ or the like is a concession to English.

Griffith

When Indra hath rejoiced with Kavya Usana, he mounts his steeds who swerve wider and wider yet.
The Strong hath loosed his bolt with the swift rush of rain, and he hath rent in pieces Susna’s firm-built forts.

Geldner

Als er sich bei Usanas Kavya g├╝tlich getan hatte, besteigt Indra die fliegenden Rosse, die besten Flieger. Der Gewaltige besteigt den eilenden Wagen, er lie├Я die Gew├дsser in Str├╢men laufen. Er sprengte die festen Burgen des Susna.

Grassmann

Wenn er beim Kavjer U├зana sich hat erfreut, besteigt die raschen, raschsten Rosse Indra dann; Aus rascher Wolke goss des Wassers Strom er aus, zerbrach des ├Зuschna feste Burgen, er voll Kraft.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou mount your chariot willingly, Indra, for the sake of drinking the libations; such as you delight in having been prepared (at the sacrifice of) ┼Ъ─Бry─Бta; be plural ased with them, as you are gratified by the effused Soma (at the sacrifices) of others, so do you obtain imperishable fame in heaven.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъary─Бta was a r─Бjaс╣Ыс╣гi, descent from Bhс╣Ыgu. Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa: he was a prince of the Mnau lineage. ┼Ъ─Бry─Бta is a descendant of ┼Ъary─Бti, the fourth son of Manu Vaivasvata. с╣Ъс╣гi Cyavana married his daughter at a solemn sacrifice attended by Indra and A┼Ыvins. Cyavana took the share of the oblations intended for the A┼Ыvins. This act made Indra angry; to appease Indra another sacrifice was prepared. The legend is cited from Kau┼Ыitaki (the legend is also noted in the Bh─Бgavata and Padma Pur─Бс╣Зas).

Jamison Brereton

You mount the chariot to the bullish drinks on which you become exhilarated at ┼Ъ─БryataтАЩs (ritual) presentation,
so that you will take pleasure in (the ceremonies) with their pressed soma, o Indra. (Then) you ascend to the unassailing signal call in
heaven.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another verse with tricky constructions. In the first p─Бda the loc. vс╣Ыс╣гap─Б╠Бс╣Зesu goes misleadingly easily into English (тАЬyou mount the chariot toтАжтАЭ like тАЬthe bus to townтАЭ). Despite my tr. I think it more likely that vс╣Ыс╣гap─Б╠Бс╣Зesu is functionally a loc. absolute of the type тАЬwhen bullish drinks (are available)тАЭ ├а тАЬon the occasion of bullish drinks / when there are bullish drinks.тАЭ In p─Бda b most tr. (Grassmann, Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) take pr├бbhс╣Ыt─Б as representing -─Бс╕е out of sandhi - following the Pp., hence a nom. pl. m. past participle - but as Oldenberg points out, this is very disruptive to the syntax. Better, with Oldenberg, to interpret it as a loc. sg. to the

-i-stem pr├бbhс╣Ыti- тАШpresentationтАЩ, a possibility suggested by Pischel (see Oldenberg) and mentioned by Geldner in his n.

P─Бda c is standardly taken as preposed to d and the verb is tr. as indicative (e.g., Geldner тАЬdu тАж deine Freude hast,тАЭ Renou тАЬtu prends plaisirтАЭ), but c─Бk├бnaс╕е is undeniably subjunctive; y├бth─Б + subjunctive regularly builds purpose clauses, which are regularly postposed. I therefore take p─Бda c with ab: the purpose of IndraтАЩs mounting of the chariot is the pleasure he will receive at the soma sacrifice.

In d all tr. take ┼Ыl├│kam as тАШfameтАЩ, but the noun refers rather to a very perceptible noise or call that signals some event. The event is often the sacrifice and the ┼Ыl├│ka-, the noise, is often issued by the pressing stones (e.g., I.113.3, 139.10, III.53.10); the noise of the ┼Ыl├│ka- is loud enough to reach to heaven (e.g., I.83.6, 190.4). This p─Бda contains this same notion of the ┼Ыl├│ka-, the audible signal of the sacrifice, going to heaven, but it seems also, oddly, to suggest that Indra follows it there. Perhaps this refers to IndraтАЩs departure to heaven at the end of the sacrifice, a common theme.

Griffith

Thou mountest on thy car amid strong Soma draughts: Saryata brought thee those in which thou hast delight.
Indra, when thou art pleased with men whose Soma flows thou risest to unchallenged glory in the sky.

Geldner

Du besteigst den Wagen zu den Stiergetr├дnkten. Dargebracht sind die Somatr├дnke des Saryata, an denen du dich berauschest. So wie du, Indra, an den somapressenden Menschen deine Freude hast, erreichst du im Himmel unbestrittenen Ruhm.

Grassmann

Bei des ├Зarjata Darbringung besteigst du auch den Wagen bei den Somatr├дnken, die du liebst, Wie Indra du bei Somabringern dich erfreust, so steigst am Himmel du zu unerreichtem Ruhm.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

English translation:

тАЬYou have given, Indra, the youthful Vс╣Ыcaya to the aged Kakс╣г─лvat, praising you and offering oblations; you, ┼Ъatakratu, were Men─Б, the daughter of Vс╣Ыс╣гaс╣Зa┼Ыva; all these your deeds are to be recited at your worship.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vс╣Ыcaya was given to Kakс╣г─лvat at a r─Бjas┼лya ceremony. Indra became Men─Б, the daughter of Vс╣Ыс╣гaс╣Зa┼Ыva and later, also fell in love with her. Men─Б is a daughter of Pitс╣Ыs by Svadh─Б and the wife of Himavat, king of mountains

Jamison Brereton

You gave little Vr╠еcay─Б to great, eloquent Kakс╣г─лvant, the soma-presser, o Indra.
You became the wife of Vr╠ес╣гaс╣Зa┼Ыva, o you of good resolve. All these (deeds) of yours are to be proclaimed at the pressings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

IndraтАЩs transformation into a human female is no more surprising than his changing into an ant in vs. 9, and is better supported. See GeldnerтАЩs note, as well as my 1991 Hyenas, where in a widespread story in Vedic prose Indra is transformed into a female hyena.

Griffith

To old Kaksivan, Soma-presser, skilled in song, O Indra, thou didst give the youthful Vrcaya.
Thou, very wise, wast Mena, Vrsanaiva’s child: those deeds of thine must all be told at Soma feasts.

Geldner

Du gabst dem alten beredten, somapressenden Kaksivat die junge Vircaya, o Indra. Du Umsichtiger hast dich in das Weibchen des Virsanasva verwandelt. Alle diese Taten von dir sind bei den Somaopfern zu verk├╝nden.

Dem grossen, frommen Dichter, dem Kakschivat, gabst zum Weib, o Indra, du die junge Vritschaja; Du, weiser, warst des Vrischana├зva Gattin einst, dies alles r├╝hmet bei den Festen man von dir.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra has been had recourse to, that he may assist the pious in their distress. Praise by the Pajras, is (as stable) as the post of a doorway. Indra, the giver of riches, who is possessed of (who desires to possess, expecting as gifts from the instrumental tutor of the ceremony) horses, cattle, chariots and wealth is present.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Pajras = Aс╣Еgirasas

Jamison Brereton

Indra has become fixed in the exclusive possession of the man of good insight; the praise song (has been fixed) like a doorpost among the
Pajras,
as it seeks horses, cows, chariots, and goods. Indra alone is master of wealth and will provide it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take p─Бda b as a nominal sentence (тАЬthe praise song is a doorpostтАЭ), but the verb of p─Бda a, a┼Ыr─Бyi тАШhas been fixed, proppedтАЩ, fits b very nicely, as Oldenberg argues. Geldner suggests such an interpretation in his notes, without rendering it in tr.

The poet Kakс╣г─лvant mentioned in vs. 13 is associated with the Pajras, who are mentioned a number of times in the hymns attributed to Kakс╣г─лvant. Elizabeth Tucker points out that p─Бda b probably contains a pun on the PN pajr├б-, which literally means тАШsturdy, steadfastтАЩ, a meaning which works well with the fixed doorpost.

I take prayant─Б╠Бin d as a periphrastic future, not a straight agent noun.

Griffith

The good man’s refuge in his need is Indra, firm as a doorpost, praised among the Pajras.
Indra alone is Lord of wealth, the Giver, lover of riches, chariots, kine, and horses.

Geldner

Indra ist jetzt in den ausschlie├Яlichen Besitz des Gutgesinnten gegeben. Wie ein T├╝rpfosten ist das Preislied bei den Pajra┬┤s, das Rosse, Rinder, Wagen, Gut heischende. Indra allein gebeut ├╝ber den Reichtum als dessen Verschenker.

Grassmann

Zuflucht ist Indra in des Frommen N├дhe, sein Lob wie Th├╝res Pfosten bei den Padschra’s, An Rossen, Rindern, Wagen reich und G├╝tern, ist Indra, Herr und Spender alles Reichthums,

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThis adoration is offered to the shedder of rain, the self-resplendent, the possessor of true vigour, the mighty; may we be aided, Indra, in his conflict, by many heroes, and abide in a prosperoud (habitation, bestowed) by you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This homage has been pronounced for the bull, the independent king, the mighty one of real unbridled force.
In this community might we, together with our patrons, be possessors of hale heroes under your protection, o Indra.

Griffith

To him the Mighty One, the self-resplendent, verily strong and great, this praise is uttered.
May we and all the heroes, with the princes, be, in this fray, O Indra, in thy keeping.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рд╕рдм рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд░рд╣ рдХрд░ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рд╣реА рдХреА рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛, рдкреВрд░реНрдгрдкреНрд░реАрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧ рдХрд░ рдкрд░рдо рдЖрдирдиреНрдж рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдФрд░ рдХрд░рд╛рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее резрел рее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдФрд░ рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдЖрджрд┐ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди, рдмрд▓рд╛рджрд┐ рдХреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐, рдЕрдиреЗрдХ рдЕрд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдХрдерди рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдз рдЕрд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдФрд░ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рддрдерд╛ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрди рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИред рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╕рднреЗрд╢ ! рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реВрд░рд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрд╡реГрд╖рднрд╛рдп рд╕рддреНрдпрд╢реБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдп рддрд╡рд╕реЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЬреЗ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдпреЗрджрдВ рдирдореЛрд╜рд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдпреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ рддрдерд╛рд╕реНрдорджрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рд░рдкреНрдпреБрдЪреНрдпрдд рдПрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдп рд╡рдпрдВ рддрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╡реГрдЬрдиреЗ рд╢рд░реНрдордиреН рд╕реНрдорддреН рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрддрдпрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рднрд╡реЗрдо рее резрел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдЧреБрдгрд╛ рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрджрдореН) рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдореН (рдирдордГ) рд╕рддреНрдХрд░рдгрдореН (рд╡реГрд╖рднрд╛рдп) рд╕реБрдЦрд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреЗрдГ рдХрд░реНрддреНрд░реЗ (рд╕реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЬреЗ) рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрддреЗ рддрд╕реНрдореИ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдзрд┐рдкрддрдпреЗ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдп (рд╕рддреНрдпрд╢реБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдп) рд╕рддреНрдпрдорд╡рд┐рдирд╢реНрд╡рд░рдВ рд╢реБрд╖реНрдордВ рдмрд▓рдВ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрд╕реНрдореИ (рддрд╡рд╕реЗ) рдмрд▓рд╛рдпред рддрд╡ рдЗрддрд┐ рдмрд▓рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежреи.реп) (рдЕрд╡рд╛рдЪрд┐) рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) рдЬрдЧрддрд┐ рдпрдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгреЗ рд╡рд╛ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдкрд░рдордкреВрдЬреНрдп (рд╡реГрдЬрдиреЗ) рд╡рд░реНрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рдпреЗрди рдмрд▓реЗрди рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНред рд╡реГрдЬрдирдорд┐рддрд┐ рдмрд▓рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежреи.реп) (рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдЪ рд╡реАрд░рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ (рд╕реНрдорддреН) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╛рд░реНрдереЗ (рд╕реВрд░рд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ (рддрд╡) (рд╢рд░реНрдордиреН) рд╢рд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣реЗред рд╢рд░реНрдореЗрддрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрей.рек) (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рднрд╡реЗрдо рее резрел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд░реНрдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреИрд░реНрднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╕реНрдпреЛрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛рдВ рдкреВрд░реНрдгрдкреНрд░реАрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдВ рдЪ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ рдкрд░рдорд╛рдирдиреНрджрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╢реНрдЪреЗрддрд┐ рее резрел рее рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рджрд┐рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд░реНрдгрдирдВ рдмрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдгрдордиреЗрдХрд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реЛрдХреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд░реНрдгрдирдВ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдЧреБрдгрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдирдВ рдЪреЛрдХреНрддрдордд рдПрддрддреНрд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЛрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореНред

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдмрд░реЛрдмрд░ рд░рд╛рд╣реВрди, рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд╕рдВрдЧ рдХрд░реВрди рдкреВрд░реНрдг рднрдХреНрддреАрдиреЗ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЪреА рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛ рдХрд░реВрди рдЖрдирдВрдж рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХреЗрд▓рд╛ рд╡ рдХрд░рд╡рд┐рд▓рд╛ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее резрел рее
